CONTEXT AND JUSTIFICATION OF THE PROJECT The Center Agro-Industrial Transformation Zone Project (PZTA-Center or Agropole-Center) is one of the flagship projects of the Emerging Senegal Plan (PSE), which embodies the strategic orientations of Senegal's economic and social policy in order to make it, by 2035, an emerging country with a united society under the rule of law. The Agropole Center is specifically aligned with pillar I of the PSE relating to the structural transformation of the economy and growth and is an integral part of the industrial component of the PSE, which provides for the establishment of five (5) integrated and competitive agropoles. The first phase of the PES, with massive public investments, led to strong growth. Its second phase has been adapted for post-COVID 19 economic recovery through the Adjusted and Accelerated Priority Action Plan of the PSE (PAP 2A-PSE 2021-2023). The PZTA-Center is the second agropolis supported by the Bank, after the Agropole-Sud approved in 2019. Etude de faisabilité de l’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 33 The Agropole-Center project covers a significant potential but little developed. It extends over the regions of Kaolack, Kaffrine, Fatick and Diourbel, for an area of 27.992 km2 and an estimated population of 4.7 million inhabitants. These provide 51.8% of national peanut production, 65.8% of millet, 41% of maize, 35% of poultry and 98% of salt production. We also note the presence in the area of the private company "Les salins du Sine Saloum" and the National Oilseed Marketing Company of Senegal (SONACOS), which are respectively the largest industrial companies producing salt for crushing and refining of the peanut oil of the country. Geographically, On the industrial level, the project fits perfectly with Senegal's industrialization strategy 2021-2035, whose axis 1 relates to the "Transformation of agricultural, forestry and fishery raw materials, for food sovereignty and exports". Ultimately, the Agropole-center will contribute to food sovereignty and the emergence of processed agricultural, forestry and fishery products with high added value on the local market and for export. Achieving this objective requires the mobilization of private direct investment on the one hand, and on the other hand, the development of an integrated ecosystem of local businesses offering products and services throughout the value chain of companies. Different targeted sectors. On the agricultural front, the Project is aligned with the National Agricultural Investment Program for Food Security and Nutrition (PNIASAN) 2018-2025, the total cost of which is estimated at CFAF 2,465 billion, articulated around 6 axes : (i) improving and securing the productive base; (ii) sustainable increase in productivity and agro-sylvo-pastoral and fishery production; (iii) the development of agro- sylvo-pastoral and fishery value chains; (iv) strengthening food security, nutritional status, resilience and social protection of vulnerable populations; (v) improvement of the business environment, governance and financing mechanisms of the agricultural and agrifood sector; (vi) strengthening of human capital. It is also aligned with the Agricultural Program for Sustainable Food Sovereignty (PASAD 2021-2023), which aims to: i) improve and secure the productive base; (ii) sustainable increase in productivity and agricultural production; iii) strengthening of the agricultural services system in terms of production support; and (iv) improving governance of the agricultural sector. From an environmental and social standpoint, the Agropole Center incorporates into its design, Senegal's commitments in terms of sustainable low-carbon development as defined in the Contribution Determined at the National Level of Senegal (CDN 2020). These commitments aim to mitigate "the current losses and damages as well as the projected impacts of climate change on arable land, hydraulic and fishery resources, likely to compromise the success of the PES", while reducing greenhouse gas emissions. (GHG) in 2025 and 2030, in the order of 23.7 and 29.5% respectively in 2025 and 2030, with the substantial support of the international community. The Agropole-center will also help implement the social component of the PSE, In terms of gender and women's empowerment, the Agropole center integrates the main gender aspects in its design, formulation and institutional governance arrangements. The development of agro- industrial value chains, sensitive to gender, technical support and capacity building to SMEs / SMIs involved in the targeted sectors, including those led by women, is planned. It is also planned to develop a strategy to facilitate the access of women and other vulnerable groups to knowledge and resources (land, inputs, equipment, lines of finance, etc.). The strengthening of SMEs and the establishment of facilities and services to support agribusiness value chains require the acquisition of a large volume of land (215 ha including 15 ha for the regional module of Medina Sabakh). This acquisition will have negative impacts on socio-economic activities and the Etude de faisabilité de l’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 34 livelihoods of the populations. Thus it was decided, in accordance with ADB safeguards and national procedures, to carry out a summary Resettlement Action Plan (RAP). 3. BRIEF DESCRIPTION OF THE PROJECT The Agro-Industrial Transformation Zone Project of the Center (PZTA-Center or Agropole-Center) is one of the flagship projects of the Emerging Senegal Plan (PSE) whose objective is to accelerate the economic and social development of Senegal, in order to '' make it an emerging country by 2035. The Project aims to contribute to the structural transformation of the economy by strengthening the country's agro- industrial transformation capacities. It covers four (04) regions (Kaolack, Diourbel, Kaffrine, and Fatick) and includes three (3) components: Component A “Strengthening agro-industrial transformation and marketing capacities”; Component B “Sustainable increase in the productivity of agro-industrial sectors”; Component C “Coordination, management and monitoring-evaluation”. Within the framework of the Agropole Center, the emphasis will be placed on favorable conditions for the development of agrifood industries in the central region of Senegal, technological mastery, strengthening of the technical and management capacity of entrepreneurs, place of financial systems in the form of Public - Private - Partnership (PPP) appropriate and marketing strategies to respond proactively to the demands / requirements of consumers and the national community in general. In addition, the Agropole Center project will allow centralized management of a shared agro-industrial infrastructure platform for multiple products and a functional manufacturing and service community. But also, it will be a driving force for regional development and industrialization, notably through the improvement of agricultural added value created at the local level. The Agropole center project will consist, among other things, in setting up a central agro-industrial transformation module, the characteristics of which are as follows: A regional transformation module: this regional module will be implemented in the Commune of Medina Sabakh located in the Department of Nioro du Rip. It is hosted by a site located in the village of Keur Sader where most of the affected people originate, in addition to the villages of Keur Ngatane, Keur Ayip and Darou Rahmane. The criteria put forward for this choice are proximity to raw materials, accessibility, proximity to en energy source, proximity to markets and connectivity to logistics and transport networks and the availability of land. This regional module will shelter specialized activities and services in the areas of administration, primary processing of agricultural products, marketing, logistics, skills and training, energy and the environment, financing and communications, maintenance and basic social services; Recommended program at the level of the regional module of Kaolack: for the development of the regional module of Kaolack planned in the Commune of Medina Sabakh (village of Keur Sader), it is recommended, within the framework of a first step, the establishment of 2 agro-industrial units, as well as a complex of agricultural product processing workshops and other related buildings. Eventually, the module will be located in a total area of 15 ha but it will initially be developed over an area of approximately 8.5 ha; The selected crops/products: at the level of the Kaolack regional module: peanuts, cereals (millet, maize and sorghum) and salt. Etude de faisabilité de l’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 35 4. OBJECTIVE OF THE RESETTLEMENT ACTION PLAN The objectives of this Abbreviated Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) of the Kaolack regional module of 15 ha in the Municipality of Medina Sabakh are the following:  minimize, to the extent possible, involuntary resettlement and land acquisition, by studying all viable alternatives from the design of the project;  ensure that affected / displaced persons are effectively consulted with complete freedom and transparency and have the opportunity to participate in all key stages of the process of developing and implementing involuntary resettlement activities and compensation;  ensure that compensation, if any, is determined in a participatory manner with people in relation to the impacts suffered, in order to ensure that no one affected by the project is disproportionately penalized;  ensure that the compensation of affected / displaced persons is made according to the full cost of resettlement;  ensure that affected people, including poor and vulnerable groups, are assisted in their efforts to improve their livelihoods and their standard and environment. 5. METHODOLOGY OF THE RAP SUMMARY ELABORATION The methodological approach adopted in the preparation of the Abbreviated RAP is based on two complementary approaches. The first is a participatory approach which combined, on the one hand, the collection and analysis of strategic documents, and on the other hand, interviews and focus groups with local actors and partners concerned by the Agropole project (services techniques of the State, administrative authorities, local elected officials, affected local populations and residents of the project). The second approach is based on a quantitative approach, based on the administration of a questionnaire and a census form to the people affected by the project activities. The objective is to identify the people and property affected and to determine the socio-economic profiles of the PAPs as well as the conditions and livelihoods of the people likely to be affected by the project, to serve as a basis for calculating the related compensation. Following these two phases conducted by the consultant, the Departmental Commission for the Census and Evaluation of Expenses (CDREI) of the Department of Nioro du Rip, set up by decree, also proceeded to the consultation of the PAPs as part of its work validation of the abbreviated RAP, through field verification of the data and information provided by the consultant (census of PAPs, assessment of losses, estimate of compensation). The CDREI then organized and supervised the conciliation session with the PAPs, which resulted in the signing of minutes of amicable agreement with the project (see annexes). 6. MAIN SOCIOECONOMIC CHARACTERISTICS OF THE LOCALITY HOSTING THE PAP The Municipality of Medina Sabakh is located in the district of Medina Sabakh, Department of Nioro du Rip, Region of Kaolack. It covers an area of 229 km2 and is limited:  In the North by the Municipality of Ngayène;  South and East by the Republic of the Gambia;  West by Paos Koto District.  In the east by the Republic of the Gambia. Etude de faisabilité de l’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 36 The Municipality of Medina Sabakh is mainly populated by Wolofs who constitute 80% of the population. The second ethnic group is composed of Halpular which represents 18% of the total population and the third group by the Mandingo which represents 2%. The total population of the municipality is 52,142 inhabitants according to RGPHAE projections 2019. The population is slightly dominated by women (50.2%) against (49.8%) men. The density is around about 534 inhabitants per km2; which is greater than the national density which is around 90 hts per km2 The predominance of women (with more than 50% of the population according to the distribution by sex) in the municipality can be explained by several factors in particular:  infant and child mortality observed more in boys than in girls. Added to this are the departures of young talibés and the migration of men in search of work in towns;  the relatively large emigration of men in the area;  the exposure of men in high-risk occupations (labor, army, etc.). The population of the Municipality is unevenly distributed over the municipal area. If almost all of the 53 villages have a large number of inhabitants, respectively by their small geographic size and by their village status, there are still demographic disparities at the village level. The big villages of Medina Sabakh which are Ndimba, Keur Ayip, Falifa, Payoma concentrate large populations with densities that exceed the municipal average. Indeed, due to its geographical position and the dynamism of trade thanks to its proximity to The Gambia and to the crossing of the RN1 connecting Dakar to the rest of the country, the massive arrival of foreigners; the town's urbanization should reach its peak in a few years (in 2035). Urbanization of the municipality should reach its peak in a few years (in 2035). The demographic development of the town will experience mixed changes in the years to come. Indeed, Medina Sabakh nowadays experiences many socioeconomic difficulties linked to the degradation of natural resources but above all to soil poverty, to the relative low standard of living of the populations among others. Thus, the agropastoral vocation of the activities of the Municipality, promotes the exodus of rural people whose homes are Senegalese urban centers, mainly Dakar, the city of Fatick and that of Kaolack. This situation is explained on the one hand by the fact that economic activities are quite simply limited to winter farming practices and increasingly vulnerable pastoral farming. This means that these sub- sectors present fewer opportunities in the generation of economic resources among the working population. Health: the commune has 04 health posts located in Medina Sabakh (center village), Ndimba, Kohel and Falifa. It also has 08 functional health huts located in the villages of Santhie Médine, Djiguimar, Payoma, Keur katim Diama, Keur sett, Sanghap, Passy rip and Keur bakka basin. There are also in the municipality 05 non-functional health huts which need to be rehabilitated in order to satisfy the health demand. Hydraulics: the municipality has infrastructures in the hydraulics sector managed collectively or individually. In addition, the quality of water is often suitable for consumption or production or both at the same time. The drinking water supply system has 08 boreholes with a large storage capacity of between 90 and 400m3 which provide service to the 58 villages and hamlets of the Commune. As part of the reform of the State of Senegal on drinking water marked by the delegation of management to water supply Etude de faisabilité de l’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 37 structures will be under the management of OFOR. The cost per m3 of water varies between a minimum of 250 FCFA and 300 FCFA at the public standpipe. The wells (more than 50 identified) are still an asset that the populations of the Municipality can exploit. The main challenge for the municipality is to cover all the villages and hamlets and provide the populations with a quality water service. Agriculture: like the department of Nioro, winter agriculture is the main economic activity in the municipality of Medina Sabakh. It holds an important position in the agricultural sector of the municipality. Agriculture is practiced by 85% of the active population of Medina Sabakh (RGPHAE 2013). From the point of view of production, the municipality is considered to be efficient. The main cereals grown in the town are: millet, cowpea, watermelon and others. Cereals represent the basis of the diet of the populations of the municipality. Note that the cultivation of watermelons has experienced an exponential rise during the last five years. Groundnuts as cash income for most of the farmers are practiced at 94% in the agricultural activities of the municipality. It represents most of the cultivated areas. Matrix of productive sectors to promote in the municipality COMMON GLOBAL SECTOR POTENTIAL STRATEGIC POTENTIAL MUNICIPALI TY OF MEDINA SABAKH Agriculture, livestock, trade  Food crops (millet, maize, cowpeas, sorghum);  Pastoral farming (Cattle, small ruminants) Market gardening, cattle and sheep fattening  Food crops (breeding intended for religious ceremonies, festivals and others) Small trade, intercommunity trade  Shops, restaurants, stables Annuity products  Related livestock activities (milk) Annuity activity  Groundnut cultivation, cattle fattening Source : CAPRODIV, August 2019 Breeding: animal husbandry is one of the dynamic economic activities alongside agriculture and commerce. It is of an extensive and traditional type and occupies the first position in terms of regeneration of economic resources for pastoralists who practice it. The herd is made up of cattle, small ruminants, horses, etc. The municipality does not have enough equipment to promote the development of the livestock sector. Apart from the communal fair which serves as a park for stray animals, no other infrastructure is present in the commune. However, the practice of this activity offers enormous advantages which can improve and positively influence the financial situation of households which are increasingly vulnerable to climatic, economic and even social factors. Trade: trade plays a very important role at the level of the municipality of Medina Sabakh. Its proximity to the Gambian Republic promotes commercial activities in the town. The greatest flows take place at the village level of Keur Ayip Gueye, which constitutes the epicenter of the commercial transaction between Senegal and The Gambia. Forest explotation: with a fairly large communal area and low density, the Municipality of Medina Sabakh has some forest rich in animal and plant products. Plant products are picked, prepared and sold to traders from Kaolack, Gambia, Dakar and other urban centers in the country. The operators do not behave like professionals; they just enforce a right of household use. Thus they have no organization Etude de faisabilité de l’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 38 and pay a tax to the water and forest services for the delivery of products such as dead wood to large cities. The few supports for the preservation and exploitation of forest products are:  the State through the Water and Forests service;  the Global Environment Facility (GEF) through its bio diversity project which helps populations in forest regeneration,  the Ecological Monitoring Center (CSE) for the recognition of ponds and bush fires With the exception of a few species resistants to human or protected pressure, all the animal and forest resources of the town are diminishing due to factors of climate change such as repeated droughts, deforestation and pruning. Mines and Industry: in the municipality there is no presence of national or international firms which are active in the industrial or mining fields. However, it is clear that the town is full of assets in this area. Quarries and other mineral resources such as limestone are present in many villages in the municipality. In addition, as part of the National Multifunctional Platforms Program, it is planned to set up platforms in villages with mineral resources. It would be appropriate for the platforms to be managed by the GPFs in order to facilitate an improvement in access to energy sources and to develop productive and income-generating activities. The industrial situation of the town: apart from low-production mechanical workshops, the town has no other significant activity in the industrial sector. The machines available on site are the millet mills. The installation of an agro-food processing plant (mile, corn and other speculant) should allow on the one hand a significant reduction in unemployment and on the other hand to stimulate the development of these crops by offering a market for them harvests. Energy: electricity is one source of energy used in the Municipality of Medina Sabakh. However, only three villages have access to electricity through the 54 official villages. These are the villages of Medina Sabakh, Ndimba Ndiayenne and Keur Ayip Gueye. As part of the action plan (2021-2025) of this Communal Development Plan (PDC), access to electricity occupies a prominent place. Access to energy is also provided by butane gas. The latter has been widely used in homes since the establishment of the nature conservation policy advocated by the State since the 1970s. However, firewood is also the most widely used source by housekeepers in the commune of Medina Sabakh. This is explained among other things by the rural character of the municipality, by its easier and less expensive accessibility and on the other hand by factorssocio-economic and even cultural. The Environment, adaptation to climate change: man remains the essential element which contributes to the degradation of the environment. The abusive cutting of trees in search of firewood and the mining of international firms remain the main factors of the environmental threat in the town. It must also be said that the practice of agriculture in the area, characterized by monoculture, ended up impoverishing the soils causing an increasingly significant drop in agricultural yields. It should be noted that speculations are developed through community gardens with significant yields. The nature of the soils consisting mainly of dior soils, favors the infiltration of rainwater, the town is not faced with flooding problems. Moreover, they are characterized by a lack of application of efficient and profitable technical routes, most often linked to an insufficient network of agricultural advisers.  Socio-economic constraints for agriculture These drawbacks essentially affect two very important aspects: the social and the economic, which are closely related to agriculture. We can mention among others:  the lack of good tracks for the transport of equipment, agricultural inputs and access to markets, especially in the department of Nioro, despite the efforts of the former PAFA and the achievements of the PUDC  insufficient storage warehouses and the dilapidated state of those that exist;  difficulties in accessing finance for small producers;  insufficient participation of a large part of the producers’ in organizational structures supposed to represent them.  the family farm is not considered by its owner as a micro, small or medium-sized agricultural enterprise that needs to be competitive and profitable. This constitutes a major handicap and prejudicial to the improvement of their results and performances. SOCIOECONOMIC IMPACTS ON THE PEOPLE AFFECTED BY THE PROJECT The main activities of the project which will generate the resettlement are essentially the release of the right-of-way during the implementation of the arrangements for the establishment of the Kaolack regional module. The impact zone includes the entire project area where activities will be carried out over 15 ha, i.e. in the Municipality of Medina Sabakh, more precisely in the villages of Santhie Sader, Keur Ngatame, Passirip and Keur Lahine. The site's land is located at the following geographic coordinates: 13.619372; -15.6117899. The project will generate considerable positive impacts on local economies. The planned activities and developments will have considerable economic impact on the populations in terms of jobs created and income generated through the use of local labor and the development of related services and activities that will boost the economy. Local economy and will be likely to fix young people in their land, or even reverse the migratory movement. In fact, 26,688 jobs are generally expected from the project, including 15,556 direct jobs. The project will strive to hire as a priority unskilled labor from the village of Keur Sader which houses the people affected by the project, but also from the villages of Santhie Sader, Keur Ngatame, Passirip, Keur Lahine and the Municipality of Medina Sabakh. In addition to the creation of direct and indirect jobs linked to the construction of the regional module, subcontracting will also facilitate permanent and temporary jobs. Improving the income of local populations will help fight poverty. The proposed developments will promote the intensification and diversification of production and consequently the increase in agricultural production. At the national level, 32.1% of households have agriculture as their primary source of income. Consequently, a significant increase in the productivity of agricultural labor will translate into a marked improvement in food security while strengthening the resilience of the targeted communities. The project will help reduce food insecurity and malnutrition in the department of Kaolack, first at the local level, then at the national level. Indeed, the project will increase the productivity of agriculture, and consequently the cereal stocks of households. It will help reduce poverty, diversify the diet and strengthen the resilience capacity of households and local communities, which will also be supported by the Agropole. The land affected by the construction of Kaolack regional module (Medina Sabakh) consists of both agricultural land and residential plots not yet built. Specifically, the project covers a total area of 15ha owned by 09 people. The project will cause these people to lose land permanently without these people having to physically move. Indeed, the census showed that no infrastructure was erected in the plots, because the PAPs did not live on the lands which are affected by the project works. LEGAL AND INSTITUTIONAL FRAMEWORK FOR RESETTLEMENT a. Legal framework for land expropriation and AfDB requirements for involuntary resettlement of populations The Summary Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) of the Agropole Center Project, more particularly that of the Kaolack regional legislation module, based on the Senegalese national law in terms of land management and expropriation for public utility and Safeguards Operational Safeguards (OS) of the African Development Bank (AfDB), in particular Operational Safeguard No. 2 (OS2) relating to "Involuntary Resettlement: land acquisition, displacement and compensation". In the event of discrepancies between the two procedures, the one that is more advantageous for the affected populations will be applied. Land tenure in Senegal and its legal texts The applicable Senegalese land legislation is made up of several texts which allow to divide the lands of Senegal into three categories which are: the national domain; the domain of the State and the domain of individuals.  National domain: the national domain is governed by law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 and its implementing decree n ° 64-573 of July 30, 1964 areas in terms of surface area and which can be used for agriculture, breeding or livestock.  Public domain: according to article 2 of the law of 76-66, the public domain of the State includes "the goods which, by reason of their nature or of the destination which is given to them, are not susceptible of private appropriation". It is divided into natural public domain and artificial public domain.  Private sector: The domain of individuals consists of registered land belonging to individuals. For a long time, it was organized by the civil code and the decree of July 26, 1932 reorganizing the property regime in French West Africa. But, in 2011, Law No. 2011-07 of March 30, 2011 on the land ownership regime repealed the previous provisions by updating the regulations to bring them into harmony with the legal arsenal in force in Senegal. The lands of the regional module of Kaolack are located in the national domain. National domain and its legal texts applicable to the project Law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 and its implementing decree No. 64-573 of July 30, 1964, are the legal texts that govern the national domain. Article 1 of the law on the national domain stipulates the following: "The national domain is automatically constituted by all land not classified in the public domain, not registered or whose ownership has not been transcribed for conservation mortgages on the date of entry into force of this law, do not automatically form part of the national domain either, the lands which, on this date, are the subject of a registration procedure in the name of a person other than the State”. Law 64-46 of June 17, 1964, in its article 4, divides the lands of the national domain into four zones which are: pioneer zones, urban zones, classified zones and terroir zones. The project lands are located in the “terroir zones”. The land area is defined in article 7 of law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 on the national domain, which stipulates that "the land area corresponds, on the date of publication of this law, to the lands which are regularly exploited for rural housing, cultivation or breeding". Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 45 Article 13 of Law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 specifies the condition for registering land in the terroirs zones. This article stipulates that “the State may only request land from the national domain constituting terroirs, or allocated by decree under article 11, for the performance of operations declared to be of public utility”. The declaration of public utility which triggers this procedure is made in the form of a decree signed by the President of the Republic of Senegal or a ministerial decree. This declaration of usefulness, which designates the area concerned, will be followed by the estimate, by the Commission for the Census and Evaluation of Expenses (CDREI) of the jurisdiction, of the compensation to be paid to the occupants. Decree 91-838 of August 22, 1991 amending law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 on the national domain, allows all occupants to be compensated. The compensation must be granted in kind or in cash. Other legal texts applicable to the project Law 11-2004 of March 26, 2004, repealing Law 76-67 of July 2, 1976, and its implementing decree, constitute the legal bases for expropriation procedures for public utility. Article 1 of this law stipulates that "expropriation is a procedure which allows the public authorities to obtain, in the form of a forced session, for its benefit, all or part of a property with a view to the realization of an objective of public utility and subject to the payment of fair and prior compensation". Article 11 of the said law, specifies that “the public utility is declared by a decree or a ministerial decree which fixes the duration of its validity, the perimeter concerned and the period during which the expropriation must be carried out”. Article 13 of Law 11-2004 of March 26, 2004 specifies the role and composition of the Commission for the Census and Evaluation of Expenses (CDREI), which essentially consists of "determining the plots to be expropriated, finding owners, holders of real property rights and other interested parties”. Law 2013-10 of December 28, 2013 on the General Code of Local Authorities is also applicable to the project, in the sense that the lands of the national domain, in particular those of the areas of the soils where the land of the regional module of Kao is located., are managed by local authorities (rural communes). At the initial stage, their availability requires an opinion from the Departmental Council and a deliberation from the Municipal Council approved by the Prefect. Article 13 of this law stipulates that, “the State may transfer to a local authority the management of part of its public domain. He may also co-manage with a local authority or assign or transfer to it, against payment or free of charge, property in his private domain located within the territorial jurisdiction of the latter. For reasons of general interest, the State reserves the right to take back all or part of these assets on condition of reimbursing the expenses in accordance with the laws and regulations. The rules relating to the classification, declassification, transfer, assignment, decommissioning and alienation of the domain of a local authority are set by law. In addition, article 31 of law 2013-10 of December 28, 2013 on local authorities, cites among the powers of the municipal council, “the allocation and decommissioning of land in the national domain”. Indeed, Law No. 2013-10 on the General Code of Local Authorities provides that for any project or operation of the State on the lands of the territorial areas of the national domain, the latter takes the decision after consulting the departmental council and of the relevant city council. AfDB Policy on Involuntary Population Displacement Regarding the AfDB's policy on involuntary displacement of populations (2003), it is operationalized through Operational Safeguard (SO) n ° 2 entitled “Involuntary Resettlement: Land acquisition, displacement of populations and compensation”. This SO aims to integrate into the Bank's operations, Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 46 the resettlement of people / populations affected by projects leading to physical and / or economic displacement. This SO aims to ensure that those who are to be displaced are treated in a fair and equitable manner, and in a socially and culturally acceptable manner, that they receive compensation and resettlement assistance so that their standard of living, their ability to generate income. The differences between Senegalese legislation and the ADB's SO2 mainly relate to the following points:  early consultation of PAPs and their participation in all stages of the resettlement process including on resettlement choices;  compensation according to the full cost of resettlement or the full replacement cost of all losses suffered;  compensation in kind for agricultural land, preferably instead of compensation in cash;  assistance to vulnerable people throughout the resettlement process through specific measures;  assistance to affected people and communities in restoring and improving their livelihoods (support measures); b. Institutional framework for resettlement in Senegal This chapter presents the institutions and structures, public or private, which have been involved to date or will be involved in the process of resettlement of the populations affected by the project. The implementation structures have been put in place in such a way as to ensure the participation of the affected populations throughout the resettlement process. Specific structures such as the presence of a support structure, the creation of a local mediation committee and the presence of a steering committee will strengthen consultation between the PAPs and the project. Institutional Arrangement and Responsibilities in the Implementation of the Abridged RAP The success of the compensation procedure will depend to a large extent on the organization that is put in place and the definition of the role and responsibilities of the institutions involved. As the contracting authority, the implementation of the Abridged PAR will be under the authority of the Ministry of Industrial Development and Small and Medium Industries (MDIPMI). Capacity assessment of institutional actors in resettlement The national structures (Town halls, Cadastre, Town planning, Estate, Agriculture, Water and Forests, Environment) involved in expropriation operations for public utility have long experience in census and compensation procedures for people affected by government projects in Senegal. These structures which operate within the framework of the Departmental Commissions of Census and Evaluation of Expenses (CDREI) set up by decrees taken by the Prefects of the area have, however, a tendency to always worked by referring to the legislative and regulatory texts which govern national expropriation procedures (Law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 on the national domain, Law 76-67 of July 2, 1976 on expropriation for reasons of utility and its implementing decree, etc.). In doing so, these CDREIs often face difficulties when they have to do the work within the framework of government projects supported by Multilateral Development Banks (MDBs) such as the World Bank and the African Development Bank (ADB) which have policies of involuntary displacement and resettlement of populations. For good reason, most of the member structures of CDREIs do not have a mastery of the principles and procedures that govern these policies for the resettlement of Technical and Financial Partners (PTF) and which are nevertheless applicable and required within the framework of operations and projects. Investment that they finance for the benefit of the State of Senegal. This is the reason why, within the framework of the implementation of the RAP Summary of the module Regional Medina Sabakh, their capacities will be strengthened to optimize their intervention in accordance with the principles and procedures of the Operational Safeguard (SO) n ° 2 of the ADB relating to “Involuntary resettlement: land acquisition, displacement and compensation of populations”. This training will focus in particular on the principles and procedures of land acquisition and the consideration of social aspects related to resettlement (consultation of PAPs to obtain their consent, application of the principle of the hierarchy of mitigation measures in the selection of sites, etc.), the procedures for surveys, inventorying, property valuation, implementation and monitoring of the Abridged RAP, etc. Key people will be identified within CDREI for knowledge sharing and transfer. 9. COMPENSATION PLAN a. Legal owners, property rights assessment and eligibility criteria In line with AfDB's SO2 on involuntary resettlement, three groups of displaced people will be entitled to compensation or resettlement assistance for the loss of land, crops, fruit trees, and income impacted by implantation of the module regional Medina Sabakh:  those who have formal legal rights to land or other property recognized under the laws of the country concerned.  those who would not have formal legal rights to land or other assets at the time of the census or assessment, but can prove that they have a claim that would be recognized by the customary laws of the country.  those who have no legal rights or recognizable claim to the lands they occupy in the sphere of influence of the project, and who do not fall into either of the two categories described above, but who, by them- themselves or via other witnesses, can prove that they occupied the sphere of influence of the project for at least 6 months before a deadline established by the borrower or the client and acceptable to the Bank. Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 47 The persons eligible under the project are made up only of natural and legal persons. Affected individual (Natural Person): an owner or operator of land for agricultural use and any other economically active person on the right-of-way who will be forced to leave or move their property and activities due to the completion of the project. These subjects constitute people affected by the project; Communities (Legal person): communities suffering collective losses due to the loss of access to the project footprint area and the loss of resources due to tree felling are also considered a category of Affected Persons by the Project (PAP) eligible for compensation (example of forest product operators). b. Census and eligibility date The eligibility deadline corresponds to the date of completion of the loss inventory operations, on which the affected assets are eligible for compensation. In the context of the said project, this date corresponds to July 18, 2021.To this end, a press release of this deadline was drafted and sent to the village chief of Keur Sader on July 14, 2021. Prior to this press release, the village chief had been previously informed by telephone and the information was already widely disseminated to potential PAPs (see Annex 3). Based on the census, the project caused the loss of 03 categories of property belonging to nine (09) PAPs. The assets affected by the project are as follows:  the loss of agricultural 15 ha of land belonging to 09 male PAPs;  the loss of 37.5 tons of peanut crops, 60 tons of cereal crops (15 tons of millet and 45 tons of maize) and 1500 bags of peanut on an area of agricultural land of 15 ha, as well as the income generated by these crops for 09 PAPs;  the loss of 17 fruit and forest trees (09 Cordyla Pinnata "Dimb", 01 Prosopis Africana "Ir" and 07 Azadirachta indica "Neem") for 04 PAPs. The four (04) vulnerability criteria below have made it possible to identify and identify vulnerable PAPs:  being a widow (woman head of household);  be aged 60 or over with no other source of income;  have a disability (motor, visual, hearing);  have 15 or more people in charge. Based on these criteria, all nine (09) PAPs were deemed vulnerable. Among them, 08 PAPs have at least 15 dependents and 01 PAP, in addition to this criterion, is aged 60 and over without any other source of income. In addition, no community loss was noted. c. Compensation principles and applicable rates The valuation will be made on the basis of the acquired value, which corresponds to the present value and which takes into account the intrinsic value of the good considered, but also the added value incorporated in it (corresponding to the general increase in cost. goods). In addition, law 64-46 of June 17, 1964 in its version amended by decree 91-838 of August 22, 1991, allows any occupant of the national domain being moved to be compensated. Cash compensation is the principle in Senegalese legislation when it comes to expropriation for public utility or withdrawal of land from the national domain. Due to the absence of a scale in the decree, the compensation offered below for information seems correct to compensate for all the damage suffered. Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 48  Land Given the constraints of land availability in the area and the risk of exacerbating land conflicts that may arise from the decommissioning of other actors for the benefit of PAPs, the Municipality of Medina Sabakh ruled out any possibility of granting land from substitution for PAPs. The lands affected by the establishment of the regional module of Medina Sabakh are therefore compensated in cash at the market price, by integrating the costs of any transactions for the acquisition of new lands and a lump sum aid of 150,000 F CFA / ha for their preparation. (Priming and fertilizing the news to reach its current level of production).  Crops Losses of annual crops (groundnuts, millet, maize) are compensated according to the annual production value (for a campaign). The value of an annual production is calculated from the estimated yield of the crop during the last campaign and the unit price of the crop on the collection market (Value of production = area (ha) X yield (kg / ha) X unit price of the product (price / kg); This information is obtained and validated by discussing with the PAPs.  Fruit trees and timber For perennial crops (fruit trees and timber), the value of production lost until the tree reaches its production phase is considered (cost of compensating fruit trees = production value X number of year until production phase). The value of production is determined as follows: average annual production per plant in kg X number of plants X value of the production of the fruit in the collection market. This information is obtained and validated by discussing with the PAPs.  Loss of income Displaced people are necessarily deprived of their sources of income for a certain period of time, ie the sale of products from crops (groundnuts, millet, maize) and timber. Even if they have new land, it takes time to develop it, cultivate it, and see the trees reach the stage of maturity and production. Based on the socio-economic survey, compensation for loss of income should be taken into account. It will cover the entire transition period and will be calculated on the basis of the daily income of the socio- professional category, whether in the formal or informal sector.  Vulnerability compensation PAPs deemed vulnerable on the basis of the four (04) criteria retained have a fixed vulnerability allowance of one (1) million CFA F, in addition to the compensations to which they are entitled. The lump sum compensation is cumulative depending on the types of vulnerability detected in the person. d. Estimation of discounted losses and their full compensation cost The basis for assessing losses and their compensation was explained to the 09 PAPs during the various consultation phases (public consultation, socio-economic surveys and inventory of affected assets, conciliation phase). Overall, the compensations as mentioned in the following tables are consistent with the full compensation costs. Their approval by the PAPs resulted in the signing of minutes of amicable agreements, under the aegis of the Commission for the Census and Evaluation of Expenses (CDREI) of Kaolack, with a conciliation rate of 100%. GRIEVANCE REDRESS MECHANISM a. Structure of GM management bodies The bodies for lodging, processing complaints and appeals are: (i) the Local Mediation Committee, (ii) the Communal Committee; (iii) Regional Coordination of the project; and (iv) justice. Each complaint management committee is independent and the complainant is free to lodge his complaint at the level of the committee of his choice.  Local Mediation Committee The Local Mediation Committee includes:  the village chief of Keur Sader, President of the local committee;  the Chiefs of the villages of Keur Ayip, Keur Ngatane and Darou Rahmane  a notable from the village of Keur Sader;  the representative of women from the village of Keur Sader;  the Representative of the youth of the village of Keur Sader;  the Representatives of PAPs from the villages of Keur Sader, Keur Ayip, Keur Ngatane and Darou Rahmane and  the Representative of the Organization of Partner Producers (OPP), Secretary of the Local Mediation Committee (CLM).  Médina Sabakh Communal Committee The Communal Committee includes:  the Mayor of the Commune of Medina Sabakh or his deputy, President of the Communal Committee;  the Chiefs of the villages of Keur Sader, Keur Ayip, Keur Ngatane and Darou Rahmane;  the Women's Representative of the Commune (GPF) of Medina Sabakh;  the Representative of the Municipal Youth Council;  the Representative of the religious and customary leaders of Medina Sabakh;  the Representatives of PAPs from the villages of Keur Sader, Keur Ayip, Keur Ngatane and Darou Rahmane;  the Representative of the OPP intervening in the area and  the Agent designated by the Town Hall for the registration of complaints, Secretary of the Communal Committee (CC).  Regional committee The Agropole Center Project has a Regional Coordination based in Kaolack within which a Regional Committee will be created in charge of recording and processing complaints. The Regional Committee includes:  the Regional Coordinator of the Agropole Center Project, President of the Regional Committee;  Infrastructure Specialists;  the Specialist of agricultural sectors;  the Environmental Safeguards Assistant; Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 54  the Social Safeguards Assistant, Secretary of the Regional Committee (CR).  Justice Recourse to judicial bodies in accordance with the provisions of the law is guaranteed by the Grievance Redress Mechanism (GRM). b. Operating process of the GRM The operating process of the GRM is presented as follows:  Receipt of complaints and doleances / acknowledgment of receipt To file a complaint, the complainant will contact the presidents or secretaries of the committees, by moving or through other channels (phone call, sms, or WhatsApp (call, voice, written)). Information concerning the contacts of the chairmen and secretaries of the Complaints Management Committees (surname and first name, function, telephone number, home address, etc.) will be communicated to potential complainants during the information and popularization phase of the MGP. All complaints received by committee chairs will be shared with secretaries and vice versa. If the complaint received by post, sms, email, or via social networks (WhatsApp) requires additional information, the complainant is contacted for the desired clarifications. In any case, upon receipt of the complaint, the president or the secretary of the committee having received the complaint, will send a return to the complainant in the form of an acknowledgment of receipt. If the receipt of the complaint is made electronically, the acknowledgment of receipt is systematically accompanied by an electronic message (sms or WhatsApp message) to ensure traceability.  Registration of complaints and grievances The complaints forwarded to the various committees will be duly recorded in a register of complaints which will be set up at the level of the committee. The secretary of each committee is responsible for registering the complaint immediately (in the event of the complainant's travel) and within two (02) days of receipt of the complaint. It will register the complaint with a confidentiality code (P01, P02, P03, etc.) which will be used to protect the identity of the complainant. The existence of this register will be widely disseminated to the populations of the area. Once the complaint has been registered, the Secretary of the committee will communicate to the complainant his confidentiality code.  Complaints handling and investigations Within two (02) days following the registration of the complaint, the secretary will send the complaint form to the chairman of the committee. The chairman of the committee will then be responsible for convening the members of the Committee within three (03) days of receipt of the complaint form from the secretary of the committee. The committee generally has a period of 15 days from the date of registration to process the complaint, i.e. 02 days for the transmission of the completed complaint form to the president, 03 days for the summons of committee members and holding the meeting and 10 days for the processing procedure. Duration of complaints handling and their reception Activity Duration Transmission of the complaint form to the committee 2 days Summons of committee members 3 days Complaint handling procedure 10 days Total 15 days Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 55 The committee will first rule on the relevance, admissibility and merits of the complaint. The assessment of the admissibility and admissibility of a complaint will be made on the basis of the criteria below:  the grievances and prejudices motivating the complaint have been verified and are real;  the grievances and harms motivating the complaint were caused by the project or its related activities;  the person is entitled to lodge a complaint because he or she is the complainant himself or an individual duly mandated by the latter (to be confirmed by the committee through its investigations). If the complaint is not admissible, it is closed with a reasoned report and the inadmissibility must be notified to the complainant with mention of the reasons which justify it. To do this, the committee will use the same channel used by the complainant to file his complaint, systematically accompanying it with a phone call to explain. If the complaint is deemed admissible, the committee will proceed with the processing. In the procedure for handling a complaint, the committee may, if it deems it necessary, hear the complainant or the persons concerned by the handling of the complaint by telephone, in order to obtain clarification or additional information which he needs. The committee seized or the persons designated by it, may also travel on site to carry out the inquiries, verifications, and investigations essential to the resolution of a complaint.  Negotiation, solution and communication of the result At the end of its processing procedure, and after consultation with the parties concerned, the chairman of the committee seized will submit to the complainant his conclusions or his proposal for a solution for adequate and fair compensation for the damage suffered within a maximum period of 30 days following the consent of the plaintiff. If the plaintiff adheres to the proposed solution, the secretary of the committee will draw up the settlement report signed by the president and the members of the committee. If the complainant does not adhere to the proposed solution, the county secretary will draw up the deficiency report signed by the chairman and the members of the committee and will suggest that he seizes the committee at the next level.  Implementation of the result For the implementation of the proposed solution and which has the support of the complainant, the chairman of the committee will send electronically the report of the settlement of the complaint and the accompanying documents (complaint form) to the Regional Coordinator of the project, for support its execution by authorized structures or persons. The chairman of the committee will then follow up on the implementation of the chosen solution, in order to report weekly to the complainant on the progress recorded by telephone or by posting using his confidentiality code, until he obtains full compensation.  Archiving and closure The committee, through its secretary, will carry out the physical and digital archiving of the documentation relating to the complaints on all the stages of the procedure, from the reception of the complaint until the repair of the damage established.  Resorting to Justice The complainant is free to have recourse to the legal system for the processing of his complaint, in particular if he has not obtained satisfaction at the level of the complaint management committees set Etude de faisabilité de l ’Agropole Centre au Sénégal Plan d'Actions de Réinstallation du Module Régional de Kaolack, Site de Médina Sabakh Version Finale IDEACONSULT International-SACI 56 up within the framework of the project. But potential plaintiffs will be informed by committee chairmen that legal proceedings are often costly, lengthy, and with no guarantee of success.  Agropole center project grievance mechanism diagram 11. Supervisory institutions and their roles The implementation of the summary RAP is the responsibility of the CEP Agropole, which will take all the necessary measures to monitor the effective and compliant execution of the resettlement and compensation measures. The internal monitoring of the implementation of the summary RAP will be ensured by the Social Safeguards Specialist (SSS) who will be able to rely in the achievement of his mission, on consultants / NGOs and the local authority of Kaolack, the Mediation Committee, and the Communal Committee at the local level as well as at the project regional coordination level. c. Dissemination of periodic monitoring and completion audit reports The Social Safeguards Specialist (SSS) of the CEP will produce monthly and quarterly reports to this effect. These reports will give an overview of the progress of the resettlement measures by comparing it with the goals and deadlines set in advance and giving explanations, if necessary, of any discrepancies between the plan and the reality. This will allow the project to plan corrective actions, if necessary, to resolve the issues. The PAR evaluation (mid-term and final) will be carried out by an independent consultant recruited by the project. This evaluation is both a performance evaluation (level of achievement of the actions planned in the RAP) and an impact evaluation. The impact assessment will highlight the impact of the project and the resettlement on the PAPs before, during, and after the project, in relation to their level of income and living. Periodic monitoring and completion audit reports will be disseminated to local stakeholders and published on publicly accessible media (website). d. Monitoring and evaluation costs The costs of monitoring and evaluation are 10,000,000 CFA francs. 12.
